<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_411377990">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411377990" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11895609-faye" class="left imgcol" title="Faye"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448813101p2/11895609.jpg" alt="Faye" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/411377990?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11895609-faye" class="user" title="Faye">Faye</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7533183-all-that-remains" title="Paperback 075153045X" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=crime-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=re-read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">re-read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=1990-1999" class="actionLinkLite">1990-1999</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=four-stars" class="actionLinkLite">four-stars</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=kay-scarpetta-series" class="actionLinkLite">kay-scarpetta-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer411377990">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10874140687561576435">First read: 2005<br /><br />Re-read: October 2015<br /><br />The plot: Kay Scarpetta is called upon to help investigate the double murder of a young couple found decomposed in the woods. Their murder appears to tie in with the double murders of several other couples who have been killed over the past few years. In this case however the young woman who was killed is the daughter of a powerful politician named Pat Harvey who has links to the CIA and the FBI. Dr Scarpetta along with Marino, Benton Wesley and Abby Turnbull</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10874140687561576435">First read: 2005<br /><br />Re-read: October 2015<br /><br />The plot: Kay Scarpetta is called upon to help investigate the double murder of a young couple found decomposed in the woods. Their murder appears to tie in with the double murders of several other couples who have been killed over the past few years. In this case however the young woman who was killed is the daughter of a powerful politician named Pat Harvey who has links to the CIA and the FBI. Dr Scarpetta along with Marino, Benton Wesley and Abby Turnbull have to decide whether Pat's daughter's murder is by the same serial killer who murdered the other couples, or whether this was a politically motivated copycat.<br /><br />What I liked:<br /><br />- As always, I love the character of Kay Scarpetta. She is smart and dedicated to her work but also very relatable and real to me.<br />- The re-introduction of Abby Turnbull. She was a journalist from book one 'Postmortem' and initially a thorn in Kay's side but they developed a nice friendship in 'All That Remains' and became a bit of a crime duo which I liked.<br />- The development of Marino's character. In the first book he seemed like a bit of a slob and a chauvinist but here it seems that Scarpetta is has softened in the way she feels about him and sympathises with him a bit more that she used to.<br />- Cornwell always manages to make it seem like the reader gets a genuine look behind the scenes at the various political machinations that must go on in real life as well as in fiction. I liked reading about the way in which the FBI were trying to control the murder investigation and hush it up, and how they had journalists in their pockets ready to discredit Pat Harvey when it seemed like she was interfering too much into the investigation of her daughter's murder.<br />- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[I especially liked that for once - aside from that one brief moment in the car with Abby - Kay had no personal interaction with the killer. He didn't become fixated on her, or try to kill her. It felt much more realistic that way! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />What I didn't like:<br /><br />- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Why did Abby have to die? I really liked her character and it was good to read about a strong female character who also had a strong female best friend. They seemed to work really well together as well. Her death definitely had a shock value but it would have been interesting to see how Abby and Kay's friendship would have evolved had she lived.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- I don't like Mark, Kay's love interest. He wasn't in the book too much but every time he was mentioned it irritated me.<br />- No Lucy again with the exception of a single phone call. <br /><br />Rating: 4/5 stars.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10874140687561576435">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_322966719">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322966719" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2747872-olga" class="left imgcol" title="Olga"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1386878842p2/2747872.jpg" alt="Olga" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/322966719?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 31, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2747872-olga" class="user" title="Olga">Olga</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/232123.All_That_Remains" title="Hardcover 9780684193953" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2747872-olga?shelf=read-in-2012" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer322966719">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7593323461024758589">Conditioned by my previous experiences with detective novels whenever I begin a Scarpetta book I expect a straightforward mystery, and every time Cornwell crafts a story that's everything but. Oh, there is a mystery alright, but there is also a very strong human element and the more I get to know Kay Scarpetta and her circle the more clearly I see it. It is possible of course that this human element is becoming more prominent, with every consecutive book being more about the people than the crim</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7593323461024758589">Conditioned by my previous experiences with detective novels whenever I begin a Scarpetta book I expect a straightforward mystery, and every time Cornwell crafts a story that's everything but. Oh, there is a mystery alright, but there is also a very strong human element and the more I get to know Kay Scarpetta and her circle the more clearly I see it. It is possible of course that this human element is becoming more prominent, with every consecutive book being more about the people than the crime, the crime being a catalyst for this humanity to manifest itself and provide a macabre backdrop for it. And you know what? I like seeing something more layered than an cold investigation into disappearances and deaths, I like seeing characters stretch themselves, doubt themselves and their friends and colleagues, struggle through life's problems and emerge changed, even just a little bit. I like seeing relationship develop through the mundane things, and Cornwell delivers that every time. In case you're wondering what it is I'm talking about: here Kay doubts her friendship with Abby Turnbull, the reporter she first met in Postmortem, because Abby isn't being particularly straightforward about her involvement in Scarpetta's latest case. It is also in this book that she realizes that the more she works with Marino the more she likes him, despite his unkempt appearance and irritating behavior, and a true friendship begins to emerge. And last but not least there are the frustrations of finding herself in the middle of basically a face-off between the FBI, the DA's office and higher echelons of government. Cornwell uses these situations wonderfully to develop her characters and since they are so significant in the story they become the stage of power plays and the really dramatic scenes. <br />Politics is big in this book and Cornwell explores the effects of it on people's lives with her usual delicate but firm touch. The potential of a cover-up in her daughter's murder case pushes a prominent politician over the edge and the question of whether she ruined her own career or was helped along the way is a major point of contention in this book. There is also the matter of whether being a public figure at a time like what this politician's family is going through is a blessing or a curse and the reality that there is more than one answer to this question. The fact that Cornwell raises these issues and that everything filters through Kay, the protagonist, makes her a complex individual who navigates a personal and professional maze every day and knows that things are much less straightforward than she would like to see, a person who regularly thinks about life and people, and not just on a simple day-to-day level. <br />My only concern with this novel is that if Cornwell continues along the path she is on the politics will grow to dominate the story and while it is a fertile field for character development I would hate to see it happen - politics tend to make things convoluted and much talk about views and positions on issues is not something I enjoy in my fiction. I think she struck a nice balance in this book and hope the next novels don't veer off into a lot of talk and little action. <br /><br />Read more of my reviews at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://bibliophilescorner.blogspot.com/">Bibliophile's Corner</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7593323461024758589">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_285420160">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285420160" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7664145-daniel" class="left imgcol" title="Daniel"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Daniel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/285420160?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 28, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7664145-daniel" class="user" title="Daniel">Daniel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/232123.All_That_Remains" title="Hardcover 9780684193953" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer285420160">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4711068694697712067">I'm in the minority, according to the reviews, but I had to put my two cents in after thoroughly reading Patricia Cornwell's novel, All That Remains.<br /><br />Although they're not the first thing I reach for when I want a good read, I quite enjoy a good intrigue/mystery novel. Jeffery Deaver's The Devil's Teardrop, for instance, impressed me quite a bit. I can appreciate a well done and suspenseful crime novel just as much as the die-hard fans.<br /><br />That having been said, I was less than impressed with this boo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4711068694697712067">I'm in the minority, according to the reviews, but I had to put my two cents in after thoroughly reading Patricia Cornwell's novel, All That Remains.<br /><br />Although they're not the first thing I reach for when I want a good read, I quite enjoy a good intrigue/mystery novel. Jeffery Deaver's The Devil's Teardrop, for instance, impressed me quite a bit. I can appreciate a well done and suspenseful crime novel just as much as the die-hard fans.<br /><br />That having been said, I was less than impressed with this book. The story line was laid out in intriguing detail and it certainly hooked my attention. And the novel never lagged or plodded like some have been known to do.<br /><br />However, I have a lot of problems with the style of the book. The dialogue, for the most part, is rather mundane. And although the story had a catchy set-up, the pay-off was rushed and lackluster. In fact, the last five or six pages were a hastily compiled series of awkward explanations for the few dangling loose ends.<br /><br />Additionally, Cornwell's prose is spare and punchy, which I normally don't have a problem with. It makes for unencumbered and breezy reading. However, she chooses to adorn the story in some odd and unnecessary spots. For instance, whenever a character is cooking, Cornwell takes great pains to detail the ingredients and manner of the meal. These descriptions are well-done, but inconsistent with the rest of the stylism, and therefore jarring and out of place.<br /><br />Finally, I understand that Cornwell has a lot of experience and inside knowledge with regards to the investigative procedures and medical examinations, which does lend the book a strong authoritative tone. However, there are times when the central character, the popular Dr. Kay Scarpetta, weighs down her speeches and conversations with lengthy and unnecessary clinical explanations. I understand that a medical examiner is naturally prone to such things, but in All That Remains, it happens often enough and clumsily enough that it begins to look less like true character development, and more like Cornwell attempting to over-authenticate the expertise found in the novel.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4711068694697712067">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_45345954">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45345954" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1068337-annabnana" class="left imgcol" title="AnnaBnana"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1217381505p2/1068337.jpg" alt="AnnaBnana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/45345954?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 04, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1068337-annabnana" class="user" title="AnnaBnana">AnnaBnana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/232123.All_That_Remains" title="Hardcover 9780684193953" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1068337-annabnana?shelf=adult-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">adult-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer45345954'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45345954">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16953080520106625978">I chose this book as one of the mysteries I'm reading for my Adult Pop Lit class, so this is long because I need to remember for discussion... <br /><br />I was compelled to keep reading this book, so I think that's saying something for good pacing and interesting plot and characters. It mostly stands up to Van Dine's 21 rules for mystery writing. <br /><br />There was a love interest for Dr. Scarpetta, but it's not at all central to the story. Because this book is a bit more of a forensic mystery, the conclusion was a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16953080520106625978">I chose this book as one of the mysteries I'm reading for my Adult Pop Lit class, so this is long because I need to remember for discussion... <br /><br />I was compelled to keep reading this book, so I think that's saying something for good pacing and interesting plot and characters. It mostly stands up to Van Dine's 21 rules for mystery writing. <br /><br />There was a love interest for Dr. Scarpetta, but it's not at all central to the story. Because this book is a bit more of a forensic mystery, the conclusion was a little unexpected, given that I don't actually know any more about forensics than what I've learned on SVU and Forensic Files. :) Cornwell gives just enough descriptive detail about her crime scenes and about what the detectives know about the crime themselves. What was a little extra compelling was that there was sort of a mystery within a mystery because Scarpetta was kept in the dark on some of the investigation. So--it was not only about solving the crime but also about figuring out what she knew and didn't know and what was accurate info and what wasn't. It kept me reading and I don't really seek out mysteries, so that's good.<br /><br />There was a bit of breaking of Van Dine's 21 mystery-writing rules--there was a bit of wonderment surrounding cigarette butts left at the scene. Also, the perpetrator of the crime is supposed to be someone who plays a more or less prominent role in the story and I didn't necessarily feel like that was the case. I wished that the killer had been introduced earlier so I would have had more of a chance of guessing who it was. Once they had a suspect, even when they thought it might not be him, it was still pretty obvious to me that it must be because there were only a couple of chapters left in the book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16953080520106625978">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7961138487741920718">The book makes a good start and PC actually went so far as to develop some of the characters. She has a great plot and some interesting characters, but they really seem to go no where.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText7961138487741920718">The book makes a good start and PC actually went so far as to develop some of the characters. I thought this book was going to be different from the first two...I was wrong.<br /><br />She did the same thing she did in the other two. She has a great plot and some interesting characters, but they really seem to go no where. Then she proceeds to lay the murders on some guy we never meet and there is no explanation for the murders. <br /><br />All we get from the book is the killer is caught or killed (usually), speculation from Kay Scarpetta, and then she just kind of shrugs her shoulders and drives away.<br /><br />This book ended horribly for me. I actually thought it was just the end of a chapter, not the end of the book. When I turned the page and saw that it was the end, I actually said, "What the hell...?" out loud. It was that much of a disappointment.<br /><br />Even though I have more of Patricia Cornwell's books in this series, I <strong>WILL NOT</strong> be reading them. As far as I am concerned, it was and would be a complete waste of my time.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_481864833">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481864833" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5903843-matt" class="left imgcol" title="Matt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444448460p2/5903843.jpg" alt="Matt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/481864833?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 11, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5903843-matt" class="user" title="Matt">Matt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/232123.All_That_Remains" title="Hardcover 9780684193953" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer481864833">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2334591573648553264">Cornwell adds another Scarpetta novel that entertains as well as educates the interested reader. After a string of couples are found murdered, miles from their vehicles, Scarpetta begins to wonder if there`s a serial killer on the loose. When a high-ranking politician turns up to be a parent to one of the slain women, the OCME (Office of the Chief Medical Examiner) kicks things up into high gear. Why were these couples chosen and why haven them leave their vehicles before killing them? How long</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2334591573648553264">Cornwell adds another Scarpetta novel that entertains as well as educates the interested reader. After a string of couples are found murdered, miles from their vehicles, Scarpetta begins to wonder if there`s a serial killer on the loose. When a high-ranking politician turns up to be a parent to one of the slain women, the OCME (Office of the Chief Medical Examiner) kicks things up into high gear. Why were these couples chosen and why haven them leave their vehicles before killing them? How long have the killings been going on and what clues lie in the earlier killings to help Scarpetta piece it all together before another couple ends up dead and miles from their abandoned vehicle? With a great plot, extremely powerful dialogue, and character development that keeps pace with the storyline, Cornwell paints an amazing medical mystery and keeps the reader begging for more. Readers just discovering this series will be looking for the entire collection before long.<br /><br />Cornwell’s novels not only portray a wonderful mystery, but also develop a thorough and intricate back story for all the characters involved. The gauge of a great author is the ability to keep the characters fresh and multi-dimensional. While the mystery must keep pace, the characters cannot live in some bubble or simply exist as though the novel is a snapshot in their lives. Cornwell does well to carry the characters through the story, but also keeps the reader apprised of their lives and personal struggles both within the novel as well as between publications. The avid reader will see past character development and see how it flourishes with each novel. There is also great use of returning characters to provide the reader with the ability to pick up previously laid threads. It is here that Cornwell’s minor character issue arises, the confusing age progression of Scarpetta’s niece, from 10 year old computer hacker to 16 year old high school sophomore. Proof that attention to detail always pays off. Behold the author’s curse of the reader who devours a series in its entirety back to back rather than reading each novel upon its release.<br /><br />Kudos, Madam Cornwell. I am a fan and cannot get enough of these books. Your ideas keep flowing and your style is superb!<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2334591573648553264">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1353392-emily" class="user" title="Emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer320035057">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8272936918978657905">A series of young couples are being abducted in the Richmond area, their bodies found months later in the woods. This leaves little for Kay to go on when determining cause of death and few clues for police to follow up. When the daughter of a prominent politician becomes one of the victims the case becomes more important than ever, but with accusations of conspiracies and cover-ups by federal agencies, the truth is even harder to find.<br />I appreciate the attention Cornwell gives to the detail of th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8272936918978657905">A series of young couples are being abducted in the Richmond area, their bodies found months later in the woods. This leaves little for Kay to go on when determining cause of death and few clues for police to follow up. When the daughter of a prominent politician becomes one of the victims the case becomes more important than ever, but with accusations of conspiracies and cover-ups by federal agencies, the truth is even harder to find.<br />I appreciate the attention Cornwell gives to the detail of the evidence and the realistic time frames involved. It seems like in books and on TV a case is solved in a matter of days. This book takes place over the course of more than a year, which is, again, a lot more congruent with actual procedure. Kay gradually becomes a more fascinating character as more of her past is revealed and she explores her relationship with FBI Agent Mark James. We also get to know a little more about detective Marino and his home life, which brings more depth to a character I haven’t been a big fan of.<br />The plot’s payoff was a little disappointing and not at all “twisty” but I was satisfied with the explanations of means and motive.<br />A decent murder mystery book for fans of the genre.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8272936918978657905">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18315553993979338706">although the novel itself is rather forgettable, the central characterization is memorable. dry, formidable, determined yet prone to various neurotic relationships (romantic &amp; otherwise), kay scarpetta is a strong creation. unfortunately the forensic science aspects take a backseat to the police procedural aspects in this entry in the long-running series. and i still can't help but question why a coroner finds herself in these various predicaments. in a novel within the 'cozy mystery' subgen</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18315553993979338706">although the novel itself is rather forgettable, the central characterization is memorable. dry, formidable, determined yet prone to various neurotic relationships (romantic &amp; otherwise), kay scarpetta is a strong creation. unfortunately the forensic science aspects take a backseat to the police procedural aspects in this entry in the long-running series. and i still can't help but question why a coroner finds herself in these various predicaments. in a novel within the 'cozy mystery' subgenre, the odd way in which protagonists often find themselves involved in mysteries is often a part of the charm; however the clinical details and chilly atmosphere of cornwell's novels are a far cry from cozy and are more mired in the challenging complexity of the superior novels of p.d. james...and so suspension of disbelief is, sadly, harder to attain.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7978760018295125881">I enjoyed the continuation of Kay Scarpetta's novel series, but felt there was something lacking from this book in places. At times it felt as if the character didn't understand her actions in a situation, which while occasionally fitting, also seemed disconnected from earlier showings of the character.<br /><br />However, that said, I did thoroughly enjoy the way that the book's plotline developed. There were changes to the personal relationships involved, between Kay and the other professionals, as well a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7978760018295125881">I enjoyed the continuation of Kay Scarpetta's novel series, but felt there was something lacking from this book in places. At times it felt as if the character didn't understand her actions in a situation, which while occasionally fitting, also seemed disconnected from earlier showings of the character.<br /><br />However, that said, I did thoroughly enjoy the way that the book's plotline developed. There were changes to the personal relationships involved, between Kay and the other professionals, as well as between Kay and her friends or lovers. Mark is a bit of a sore spot during this book, and I think that it was handled in a way very fitting to Dr Scarpetta's personality. However, Abby, and the ending of the book, seemed to let the narrative down somewhat. The earlier version of her character do not match with the one in this book, or at least, that is my feeling.<br /><br />I am looking forward to reading the next book, and hopefully, seeing Dr Scarpetta end a book without some sort of massive emotional trauma.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12077347024429316737">Hace varios años compré una novela en bolsillo de serie negra. Recuerdo que la leí, me tuvo entretenida e incluso llegué a comprar otra novela de la misma autora, que nunca llegué a leer. Hasta ahí toda mi relación con Patricia Cornwell.<br /><br />No podría decir por qué no volví a leer una novela suya. No son obras maestras de la literatura, pero para mí, la idea de un buen libro es aquel que te absorbe y te hace olvidar que el mundo existe durante el rato que dura la lectura. Y, en ese sentido, cumplen s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12077347024429316737">Hace varios años compré una novela en bolsillo de serie negra. Recuerdo que la leí, me tuvo entretenida e incluso llegué a comprar otra novela de la misma autora, que nunca llegué a leer. Hasta ahí toda mi relación con Patricia Cornwell.<br /><br />No podría decir por qué no volví a leer una novela suya. No son obras maestras de la literatura, pero para mí, la idea de un buen libro es aquel que te absorbe y te hace olvidar que el mundo existe durante el rato que dura la lectura. Y, en ese sentido, cumplen sobradamente su función.<br /><br />El caso es que ayer me tropecé con una oferta en el supermercado y pude comprar una pequeña pila de novelas de serie negra a un precio bastante económico. Varias de ellas de Patricia Cornwell y por este triste motivo, he decidido reconciliarme con ella y leerme su serie dedicada a la Doctora Scarpetta.<br /><br />Comencé con La Jota de Corazones, porque es el primero que tengo en orden cronológico y creo que me ha gustado más que el libro que leí hace unos años. Al menos, la otra vez no leí más libros de la autora y ahora planeo leer una serie completa de la misma. Eso sí, no sé si fue el libro o fuí yo, que cambié durante los años...<br /><br />Los personajes de la novela, comenzando por su protagonista, la Doctora Scarpeta me parecen bien construidos. Y la trama, que en esta ocasión se basa en la persecución a un psicópata que asesina a parejas jóvenes tiene interesantes picos de acción y vueltas de tuerca, por lo que me parece un libro bastante recomendable. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12077347024429316737">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7488895987240261088">All That Remains is a decent crime novel that develops into quite a good read after a fairly slow start. This book was quite a change of pace from the two thriller novels that I've read recently. All That Remains is far less action-packed than these other books, with more attention given to the gradual development of the characters and plotline. I really appreciate the work that Patricia Cornwell put into these aspects of her book. The detailed dialogue between characters was also a feature and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7488895987240261088">All That Remains is a decent crime novel that develops into quite a good read after a fairly slow start. This book was quite a change of pace from the two thriller novels that I've read recently. All That Remains is far less action-packed than these other books, with more attention given to the gradual development of the characters and plotline. I really appreciate the work that Patricia Cornwell put into these aspects of her book. The detailed dialogue between characters was also a feature and a real strength of this novel. On the whole, this novel was really enjoyable to read, and ended up exceededing my expectations after its slow start.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12741085405125017379">I can't get over what a gripping read this book is. I mean, setting aside the regrettable cover art, how is it that forensic science has aged more than twenty years since this novel was written but ALL THAT REMAINS never feels the least bit dated? Here, Cornwell achieves a near-perfect balance between time spent in a forensic lab and out on the street engaging in good old-fashioned detective work. She also does a great job with character development, especially by handling Carpetta's love life i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12741085405125017379">I can't get over what a gripping read this book is. I mean, setting aside the regrettable cover art, how is it that forensic science has aged more than twenty years since this novel was written but ALL THAT REMAINS never feels the least bit dated? Here, Cornwell achieves a near-perfect balance between time spent in a forensic lab and out on the street engaging in good old-fashioned detective work. She also does a great job with character development, especially by handling Carpetta's love life in a way that seems both realistic and mature. The plot is inventive and unpredictable, the writing lean and efficient. Yes, the ending may strike you as rather less than perfect, but one can't have everything, right? </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12267941688585929934">This series is what I call a "guilty pleasure". Not at all high-brow, but easy to read thrillers with some mystery, and I have to admit that I enjoy the gruesome details about forensic pathology. She makes me nuts sometimes when she does risky t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12267941688585929934">This series is what I call a "guilty pleasure". Not at all high-brow, but easy to read thrillers with some mystery, and I have to admit that I enjoy the gruesome details about forensic pathology. Being an engineering type, I like to know the details behind things, how things work, in particular when it comes to problem solving or investigative techniques.<br /><br />I do love the character of Kay Scarpetta; she's a strong, smart woman who is also attractive. She makes me nuts sometimes when she does risky things that her superior brain should be telling her not to do, but then there wouldn't be a story, would there?</span>

Especially to the illustrious Pat Harvey, mother of the last slain girl and the national "drug czar" of the federal government. Is the FBI withholding vital information from Scarpetta? Is someone inside the CIA committing these murders? Is so, why? And how is her friend, Abby, involved?</span>

      <a href="/user/show/2410586-john-carter-mcknight" class="user" title="John Carter McKnight">John Carter McKnight</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1440746227">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14758986690757616698">I haven't read Cornwell in about 20 years: found this in the depths of my Kindle directory without realizing it was one of her first books. I was a bit underwhelmed: the plot is super, the denouement exciting and shocking, but the prose trudged. <br /><br />Somebody's killing couples along the Richmond, Virginia roadside: somehow they're leaving their cars apparently willingly, only to be found dead and barefoot in the woods months later. When one of the couples includes the daughter of the Federal drug cza</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14758986690757616698">I haven't read Cornwell in about 20 years: found this in the depths of my Kindle directory without realizing it was one of her first books. I was a bit underwhelmed: the plot is super, the denouement exciting and shocking, but the prose trudged. <br /><br />Somebody's killing couples along the Richmond, Virginia roadside: somehow they're leaving their cars apparently willingly, only to be found dead and barefoot in the woods months later. When one of the couples includes the daughter of the Federal drug czar, things step up: she's convinced the FBI is covering up knowledge that the killer is CIA, and in return the FBI is seriously gaslighting her. <br /><br />It's a terrific setup. And it's a fine book, an excellent insomniac night's diversion. It just...didn't shine.<br /><br />Observations: it's amazing anybody ever got anything done before smartphones and the internet. One particularly memorable bit involves Scarpetta trying to find who wrote a prescription for one of the victims. She calls a friend in another town, has them photocopy the "pharmacy" section of the local yellow pages and fax them to her, then gets a bunch of people together to call each one to ask if the pharmacist *remembers* the victim. <br /><br />Also, rampant genteel homophobia, which as I read on in the series is a recurring theme. And smoking, everywhere, including in restaurants. You kind of expect gladiators and bloodletting. In retrospect, it's amazing how much culture has changed in 20 years. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14758986690757616698">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1698096088874361618">Als grote fan van de boeken van Karin Slaughter - die ik allemaal in een recordtempo verslonden heb - was ik al een tijdje op zoek naar een waardig alternatief. Ik had wel al eens gehoord van Patricia Cornwell en de reeks rond Kay Scarpetta, maar eerlijk gezegd liet ik mij een beetje afschrikken door wat iemand op een forum schreef, nl. dat de eerste boeken (die zich begin de jaren '90 afspelen) wat gedateerd zouden zijn. Lange tijd hield ik de boot dus af... Wat ben ik blij dat ik er uiteindeli</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1698096088874361618">Als grote fan van de boeken van Karin Slaughter - die ik allemaal in een recordtempo verslonden heb - was ik al een tijdje op zoek naar een waardig alternatief. Ik had wel al eens gehoord van Patricia Cornwell en de reeks rond Kay Scarpetta, maar eerlijk gezegd liet ik mij een beetje afschrikken door wat iemand op een forum schreef, nl. dat de eerste boeken (die zich begin de jaren '90 afspelen) wat gedateerd zouden zijn. Lange tijd hield ik de boot dus af... Wat ben ik blij dat ik er uiteindelijk toch aan begonnen ben ! Ik gaf de twee eerste boeken destijds ook al 5 sterren, en dat is met dit derde deel niet anders. Mooie vooruitzichten met nog 19 delen te gaan !<br /><br />Gedateerd zijn de boeken allerminst. Het is waar dat er op gebied van forensisch sporenonderzoek, maar ook op allerlei andere gebieden (computer, telefonie, internet,...) een grote (r)evolutie geweest is de laatste 25 jaar. Maar ik heb deze veranderingen zelf beleefd en vind er niets gedateerd aan. Neem nu bijvoorbeeld de semafoon : in de jaren '90 was dat hip. Ik vind het juist fijn om deze evoluties allemaal nog eens te beleven in een boekenreeks. <br /><br />De diehard fans van Slaughter kan ik verder alleen maar aanraden om Cornwell ook eens te proberen. Persoonlijk hou ik zelfs nog meer van de boeken van Cornwell omdat ze meer "to the point" zijn. In de boeken Slaughter zit naast de misdaden ook een liefdesverhaal verwerkt, en soms leidt dat de aandacht af. Bij Cornwell ligt de focus op het "crime" aspect. Haar schrijfstijl doet mij trouwens erg vaak aan die van Slaughter denken. Maar Cornwell's eerste boek verscheen in 1990, dat van Slaughter pas in 2001...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1698096088874361618">...more</a>

                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1461818443">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7609467645329750487">Ok with this I would definitely go for more Scarpetta Books.<br /><br />This is my first Cornwell book. I wanted to start with Post Mortem but since I couldnt grab a copy of that , I researched on her books that had good reviews and luckily All that Remains is of them.<br /><br />The books moves in a gripping pace, with an interesting plot where young teenagers are targeted and murdered and the bodies dont turn up until later. Dr Kay Scarpetta, the lead heroine, is a forensic technician who works on the dead bodies. Sh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7609467645329750487">Ok with this I would definitely go for more Scarpetta Books.<br /><br />This is my first Cornwell book. I wanted to start with Post Mortem but since I couldnt grab a copy of that , I researched on her books that had good reviews and luckily All that Remains is of them.<br /><br />The books moves in a gripping pace, with an interesting plot where young teenagers are targeted and murdered and the bodies dont turn up until later. Dr Kay Scarpetta, the lead heroine, is a forensic technician who works on the dead bodies. She also performs the role of a little 'detective' and helps in unwinding the mystery.<br /><br />There are a lot of medical terms involved which is a little difficult to understand for a layman ( I love medicine and it didnt matter to me much though i had to google every now and then!). The last few pages was a bit of a let down since the killer comes out all of a sudden and its by mere accident that Kay tracks him. He is a mystery until 80% of the book. But i definitely appreciate the way Kay tracks down the killer!<br /><br />After seeing many detective pairs in the course of my reading, Kay-Marino is surely one of them in my favorites !!<br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1233948322">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6012151891763447775">Junge Pärchen werden von einem psychopathischen Serienkiller hingerichtet, und so gut versteckt, dass sie erst etliche Monate später gefunden werden. Der Fall erlangt schon bald hohe Aufmerksamkeit in den Medien, als sich die Tochter einer berühmten Drogenbeauftragten unter den Opfern befindet.<br /><br />„Das Fünfte Paar“ ist ein gut durchdachter Roman mit einigen exzellenten und nicht vorhersehbaren Überraschungen und Wendungen. Ich habe zuvor noch nie einen Kay Scarpetta-Roman gelesen und war eindeutig p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6012151891763447775">Junge Pärchen werden von einem psychopathischen Serienkiller hingerichtet, und so gut versteckt, dass sie erst etliche Monate später gefunden werden. Der Fall erlangt schon bald hohe Aufmerksamkeit in den Medien, als sich die Tochter einer berühmten Drogenbeauftragten unter den Opfern befindet.<br /><br />„Das Fünfte Paar“ ist ein gut durchdachter Roman mit einigen exzellenten und nicht vorhersehbaren Überraschungen und Wendungen. Ich habe zuvor noch nie einen Kay Scarpetta-Roman gelesen und war eindeutig positiv überrascht. Ich habe dieses Buch innerhalb eines Tages verschlungen.<br /><br />Einzig und allein das Ende hat mich ein bisschen enttäuscht. Es kam mir so vor, als hätte sich die Autorin anfangs sehr viel Zeit genommen um alles genauestens zu beschreiben und den Leser/die Leserin mehrmals in die Irre zu führen, und schlussendlich schien sie es doch eiliger zu haben und alles kam sehr schnell zu einem Ende - und viele Fragen blieben leider unbeantwortet.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6012151891763447775">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/105081200?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 11, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1392376-erin" class="user" title="Erin">Erin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/232123.All_That_Remains" title="Hardcover 9780684193953" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1392376-erin?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer105081200">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12581148813317016150">UGH! I was trucking along, really enjoying the story, and then the last 2 or 3 chapters hit. And they were lame. It was almost as if the author was typing and realized she needed to get to the grocery store before it closed, so she decided to end the book and call it a day. Terrible ending!<br /><br />Still, I will read the others in this series because I liked the characters and the story, until the very end.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/27021963-vivi-vocat" class="left imgcol" title="Vivi Vocat"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1443516330p2/27021963.jpg" alt="Vivi Vocat" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/801235545?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 05, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/27021963-vivi-vocat" class="user" title="Vivi Vocat">Vivi Vocat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/232123.All_That_Remains" title="Hardcover 9780684193953" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/27021963-vivi-vocat?shelf=forensic" class="actionLinkLite">forensic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer801235545">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14677541910118477849">I was hooked from page one. The story line was laid out in intriguing detail (loving the recipes.<br /><br />The plot threw curve balls to the Reader and never lagged or plodded.<br /><br />There is no lofty language, the prose is spare and punchy, but the man-are-stupid-untidy-brutes tone of this book was quite irritating at some points.<br /><br /><br />Overall this book is good, for unencumbered and breezy reading.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/159833-jaime?shelf=suspense" class="actionLinkLite">suspense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer22768668">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17615943984082943846">It’s interesting to read these early books in the series after reading a lot of the later ones. Fills in the blanks on some of the back story. Overall, this one was pretty good, though there was some stuff jumped over in the end, like Cornwell didn’t want to go over a certain number of pages, so she just refers to it instead of actually writing about it.</span>

          </span>

//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EhWCbUuD84Xlp8uugAn6UxvIl5HV6yiz5I1YXkQlgVd3wb2+uVHnf2l/vxX+aBzhUj9UiJw2bxmOhF3MiLB3Eg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+2g4Rb2RyFd9pq/fiJWJXuxDaBxQh764PGFqU/iQZF6evAeWT0PcrfF+22T29G/spbSrBRla+RJWaG/BNAWSGw==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

Now in Kellerman\'s most compelling and powerful novel yet, L.A. psychologist-detective Alex Delaware confronts a long-unsolved murder of unspeakable brutality -- an ice-cold case whose resolution threatens his survival, and that of longtime friend, homicide detective, Milo Sturgis.\n\nThe nightmare begins when Alex receives a strange package in the mail with no return address. Inside is an ornate album filled with gruesome crime scene photos -- a homicide scrapbook entitled The Murder Book. Alex can find no reason for anyone to send him this compendium of death, but when Milo views the book, he is immediately shaken by one of the images: a young woman, tortured, strangled, and dumped near a freeway ramp. This was one of Milo\'s first cases as a rookie homicide cop: a vicious killing that he failed to solve, because just as he and his training partner began to make headway, the department closed them down. Being forced to abandon the young victim tormented Milo. But his fears prevented him from pursuing the truth, and over the years he managed to forget. Or so he thought.\n\nNow, two decades later, someone has chosen to stir up the past. As Alex and Milo set out to uncover what really happened twenty years ago, their every move is followed and their lives are placed in jeopardy. The relentless investigation reaches deep into L.A.\'s nerve-centers of power and wealth-past and present. While peeling back layer after layer of ugly secrets, they discover that the murder of one forgotten girl has chilling ramifications that extend far beyond the tragic loss of a single life.\n\nA classic story of good and evil, sacrifice and sin, The Murder Book is a gripping page-turner that illuminates the darkest corridors of the human mind. Adding to the city\'s woes is a series of shocking crimes, in which wealthy men are made to watch while their wives are brutalized. A sadistic demand that ends in abduction and death.The pattern suggests one man: serial killer Warren Hoyt, recently removed from the city\'s streets. Police can only assume an acolyte is at large, a maniac basing his attacks on the twisted medical techniques of the madman he so admires. At least that\'s what Detective Jane Rizzoli thinks. Forced again to confront the killer who scarred her - literally and figuratively - she is determined to finally end Hoyt\'s awful influence . . . even if it means receiving more resistance from her all-male homicide squad.But Rizzoli isn\'t counting on the U.S. government\'s sudden interest. Or on meeting Special Agent Gabriel Dean, who knows more than he will tell. Most of all, she isn\'t counting on becoming a target herself, once Hoyt is suddenly free, joining his mysterious blood brother in a vicious vendetta. . . .Filled with superbly created characters and the medical and police procedural details that are her trademark,The Apprentice is Tess Gerritsen at her brilliant best. Set in a stunning world where evil is easy to learn and hard to end, this is a thriller by a master who could teach other authors a thing or two.From the Hardcover edition.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell">About Patricia Cornwell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell"><img alt="1025097" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1442522626p2/1025097.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer13707836856913580821">Patricia Cornwell sold her first novel, Postmortem, in 1990 while working as a computer analyst at the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner in Richmond, Virginia. Postmortem, was the first bona fide forensic thriller. It paved the way for an explosion of entertainment featuring in all things forensic across film, television and literature. <br /><br />Postmortem would go on to win the Edgar, Creasey, Anthony,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13707836856913580821">Patricia Cornwell sold her first novel, Postmortem, in 1990 while working as a computer analyst at the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner in Richmond, Virginia. Postmortem, was the first bona fide forensic thriller. It paved the way for an explosion of entertainment featuring in all things forensic across film, television and literature. <br /><br />Postmortem would go on to win the Edgar, Creasey, Anthony, and Macavity awards as well as the French Prix du Roman d’Aventure prize – the first book ever to claim all these distinctions in a single year. To date, Cornwell’s books have sold some 100 million copies in thirty-six languages in over 120 countries. She’s authored twenty-nine New York Times bestsellers.<br /><br />Patricia’s novels center primarily on medical examiner Kay Scarpetta along with her tech-savvy niece Lucy and fellow investigator Pete Marino. Celebrating 25 years, these characters have grown into an international phenomenon, winning Cornwell the Sherlock Award for best detective created by an American author, the Gold Dagger Award, the RBA Thriller Award, and the Medal of Chevalier of the Order of Arts and Letters for her contributions to literary and artistic development. <br /><br />Fox 2000 bought the rights to Kay Scarpetta. Working with producer Liz Friedman, Marvel’s Jessica Jones and fellow Marvel EP and Twilight Saga scribe Melissa Rosenberg to develop the film and find Scarpetta a home on the big screen. <br /><br />After earning her degree in English from Davidson College in 1979, she began working at the Charlotte Observer. <br /><br />Cornwell received widespread attention and praise for her series of articles on prostitution and crime in downtown Charlotte. From the Charlotte Observer, Cornwell moved to a job with the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner of Virginia – a post she would later bestow upon the fictional Kay Scarpetta. <br /><br />When not writing from her Boston home, Patricia tirelessly researches cutting-edge forensic technologies to include in her work. Her interests span outside the literary: Patricia co-founded of the Conservation Scientist Chair at the Harvard University Art Museums. She appears as a forensic consultant on CNN and serves as a member of Harvard-affiliated McLean Hospital’s National Council, where she advocates for psychiatric research. She’s helped fund the ICU at Cornell’s Animal Hospital, the scientific study of a Confederate submarine, the archaeological excavation of Jamestown, and a variety of law enforcement charities. Patricia is also committed to <br />funding scholarships and literacy programs. Her advice to aspiring authors: “Start writing. And don’t take no for an answer.” <br /><br /><br />Social and Digital Outlets<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.patriciacornwell.com" target="_blank">http://www.patriciacornwell.com</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/patricia.cornwell" target="_blank">https://www.facebook.com/patricia.cor...</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/1pcornwell" target="_blank">https://twitter.com/1pcornwell</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://instagram.com/1pcornwell/" target="_blank">https://instagram.com/1pcornwell/</a><br /><br /><br />Other areas of expertise &amp; interests<br />Forensics | Forensic Technologies | Ballistics | Weapons | Explosives | Pathology &amp; Autopsies | Crime | Historical and Unsolved Criminal Cases | Jack The Ripper | Helicopter Piloting | Suba Diving | Archaeological Excavation Experience |</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13707836856913580821">...more</a>

    </div>

That\'s w&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText4934565253244101647\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;See alternate cover edition here\n\nVirginia Medical Examiner Kay Scarpetta has a bloody puzzle on her hands: five headless, limbless cadavers in Ireland, plus four similar victims in a landfill back home. Is a serial butcher loose in Virginia? That\'s what the panicked public thinks, thanks to a local TV reporter who got the leaked news from her boyfriend, Scarpetta\'s vile rival, Investigator Percy Ring. But the butchered bodies are so many red herrings intended to throw idiots like Ring off the track. Instead of a run-of-the-mill serial killer, we\'re dealing with a shadowy figure who has plans involving mutant smallpox, mass murder, and messing with Scarpetta\'s mind by e-mailing her gory photos of the murder scenes, along with cryptic AOL chat-room messages. The coolest innovation: Scarpetta\'s gorgeous genius niece, Lucy, equips her with a DataGlove and a VPL Eyephone, and she takes a creepy virtual tour of the e-mailed crime scene.\n\nUnnatural Exposure boasts brisk storytelling, crackling dialogue, evocative prose about forensic-science sleuthing, and crisp character sketches, both of familiar characters like Scarpetta\'s gruff partner Pete Marino and bit players like the landfill employee falsely accused by Ring. Plus, let\'s face it: serial killers are old hat. Cornwell\'s most vivid villains are highly plausible backstabbing colleagues like Ring, who plots to destroy Lucy\'s FBI career by outing her as a lesbian. Some readers object to the rather abrupt ending, but, hey, it\'s less jarring than Hannibal\'s, and it\'s the logical culmination of Cornwell\'s philosophy about human nature. To illuminate the novel\'s finale, read Cornwell\'s remarks on paranoia in her Amazon.com interview. --Tim Appelo&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"4934565253244101647\" href=\"#\"
